## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship of a material. Stress typically increases nonlinearly with strain and decreases with temperature due to thermal softening and thermally activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic deformation, Hollomon equation)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (nonlinear stress-strain with saturation)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Linear thermal softening with power hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (combined hardening and softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (exponential temperature dependence)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * exp(-c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal activation)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Sellars-Tegart / Garofalo creep model)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Combined Ludwik-thermal: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (full constitutive with Arrhenius softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (concave-down stress-strain curves) → power-law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturating forms like 1-exp(-c*epsilon)
- Thermal softening (stress decreases with temperature) → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n) or exp(-c*T) applied to stress
- Thermally activated deformation mechanisms → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms reflecting Boltzmann statistics
- Yield stress (nonzero stress intercept at small strain) → additive constant c0 in stress expression, e.g., c0 + f(epsilon)
- Stress saturation at large strains → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational forms epsilon/(epsilon + c)
- Homologous temperature scaling → stress depends on T/T_melt ratio, appearing as c0*(1 - c1*T) with c1 encoding melting point
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → piecewise or smooth crossover: c0*epsilon for small epsilon transitioning to c1*epsilon**c2
- Strain-temperature coupling → cross terms like epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 capturing interaction between hardening and softening

```
96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*(T - 352.18) + 1) - 0.4785*(T - 352.18) + 8.062*(T - 352.18)*log(epsilon + 1)
```

Expanding:
- First term: `96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*T + 0.00975*352.18 + 1)` = `96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*T + 4.4338)` = `-0.9443*epsilon*T + 429.37*epsilon`

- Third term: `8.062*T*log(epsilon+1) - 8.062*352.18*log(epsilon+1)` = `8.062*T*log(epsilon+1) - 2839.5*log(epsilon+1)`

So GT = `-0.9443*T*epsilon + 429.37*epsilon - 0.4785*T + 168.57 + 8.062*T*log(epsilon+1) - 2839.5*log(epsilon+1)`

The key structural components are:
1. `T*epsilon` term (linear)
2. `epsilon` term (linear)
3. `T` term (linear)
4. Constant term
5. `T*log(epsilon+1)` term
6. `log(epsilon+1)` term

So I need: **T*epsilon, epsilon, T, constant, T*log(epsilon+1), log(epsilon+1)**

The critical hard-to-match term is `T*log(epsilon+1)`. Let me check which candidates can produce this.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*(T - 352.18) + 1) - 0.4784*(T - 352.18) + 8.062*(T - 352.18)*log(epsilon + 1)
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*T + 0.00975*352.18 + 1)` = `96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*T + 3.4338 + 1)` = `96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*T + 4.4338)`
  - = `96.829*(-0.00975)*epsilon*T + 96.829*4.4338*epsilon`
  - = `-0.9441*epsilon*T + 429.24*epsilon`

- Second term: `-0.4784*(T - 352.18)` = `-0.4784*T + 168.56`

- Third term: `8.062*(T - 352.18)*log(epsilon + 1)` = `8.062*T*log(epsilon+1) - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)`

So GT = `-0.9441*epsilon*T + 429.24*epsilon - 0.4784*T + 168.56 + 8.062*T*log(epsilon+1) - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `epsilon*T` (bilinear term)
2. `epsilon` (linear in epsilon)
3. `T` (linear in T)
4. constant
5. `T*log(epsilon+1)` 
6. `log(epsilon+1)`

This is a function with terms: `a*epsilon*T + b*epsilon + c*T + d + e*T*log(epsilon+1) + f*log(epsilon+1)`

Now I need to check each candidate to see if it can produce these exact basis functions.

Let me check candidates systematically. The key distinguishing features are:
- The `epsilon*T` bilinear term
- The `T*log(epsilon+1)` term
- No exponential functions (exp)
- No sin functions

Any candidate with `exp(T*c)` or `exp(c/T)` or `sin()` terms that cannot be zeroed out while maintaining the required structure will not match.

Let me focus on candidates that could potentially match.

**Key observation:** The GT requires `T*log(epsilon+1)` which is a product of T and log. Very few candidates have this structure. Let me look for candidates that have T multiplied by log terms or can produce such terms.

Looking through candidates, most have structures like `exp(T*c)`, `exp(c/T)`, `sin(...)`, `epsilon**c`, etc. These cannot produce `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

Let me check candidates that have `T*` multiplied by functions of epsilon:

**Candidate 3:** `T*c0*(c1 + epsilon)**2 + c2*epsilon*exp(T*c3) + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon + c7`
- `T*(c1+epsilon)^2 = T*(c1^2 + 2*c1*epsilon + epsilon^2)` — this gives `T*epsilon^2` which GT doesn't have. Can't zero the T*epsilon^2 without zeroing everything. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 40:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*exp(T*c2) + c3*epsilon + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon + c7`
- Has `T*epsilon` but needs `T*log(epsilon+1)` — missing. If we set c2=0, exp becomes constant, giving: `T*c0*epsilon + const + (c3+c6)*epsilon + c4*log(c5*epsilon+1) + c7`. This has `T*epsilon`, `epsilon`, `log(epsilon+1)`, constant, but missing `T*log(epsilon+1)` and `T`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 58:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*exp(c3/T) + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon + c7`
- Has `T*epsilon`, `T`, `log(epsilon+1)`, `epsilon`, constant, and `exp(c3/T)`. Missing `T*log(epsilon+1)`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 65:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*exp(c2/T) + c3*epsilon + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon + c7`
- Missing `T*log(epsilon+1)` and `T`. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 66:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon*exp(c2/T) + c3*epsilon + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon + c7`
- Missing `T*log(epsilon+1)`. NO MATCH.

None of the candidates contain a `T*log(epsilon+1)` term, which is essential in the GT and cannot be produced from any other basis functions.

Let me verify every single candidate... After careful review, **no candidate** has a term of the form `T*log(epsilon + c)`, which is required by the GT.
